## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of concentration change in a chemical reaction. The rate dA/dt is fundamentally governed by the concentration A through rate laws of various orders, with possible explicit time dependence indicating complex mechanisms, time-varying conditions, or catalytic effects.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate dependence)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A) (transition between first and zero order)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (product-catalyzed, logistic-type rate)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reactions with equilibrium)
- Parallel reactions: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (sum of first and second order pathways)
- Time-dependent rate constant: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (rate constant changing with time, e.g., temperature ramp)
- Catalyst deactivation: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (exponential decay of catalytic activity)
- Power-law with time modulation: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (fractal or diffusion-limited kinetics)
- Sigmoidal rate law: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (A**c1 + c2) (cooperative kinetics)
- Square root kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**0.5 (half-order, surface or chain reactions)
- Competitive inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (1 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2) (complex adsorption/inhibition)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Simple power-law dependence on concentration → nth-order rate law dA_dt = c*A^n, common in elementary reactions
- Rate approaching a constant at high concentration → saturation kinetics with rational form A/(1+c*A), indicating surface or enzyme-limited processes
- Quadratic dependence on concentration with sign change → autocatalytic or equilibrium-approaching behavior dA_dt = c*A*(c-A)
- Explicit time dependence in rate expression → non-isothermal conditions, catalyst deactivation, or photochemical intensity variation
- Fractional power of concentration (e.g., A^0.5) → chain reaction mechanisms or surface-mediated reactions where intermediates are in steady state
- Sum of multiple power-law terms in A → parallel reaction pathways consuming the same reactant
- Rate that changes sign at a specific concentration → reversible reaction approaching equilibrium, dA_dt = c0*A + c1
- Product of power of A and power/exponential of t → diffusion-limited or aging kinetics in heterogeneous systems
